LABOR AND DELIVERY GROUP B STREPTOCOCCAL PROPHYLAXIS ORDERS

ALLERGIES: WEIGHT:

HEIGHT:

Perinata! Group B Streptococcus (GBS ) Prophylaxis Indicated if ANY of the following conditions are met:

Positive GBS screening culture (vaginal and/or rectal) at 35-37 weeks gestation (unless a planned cesarean delivery, in the absence of labor or amniotic membrane rupture, is performed) OR Previous infant with invasive GBS disease OR GBS bacteriuria during current pregnancy OR

Unknown GBS status (culture not done, incomplete, or resutts unknown) and ANY of the following conditions apply:

¢ Delivery at less than 37 weeks gestation

« Amniotic membrane rupture greater than 18 hours

e Intrapartum temperature 100.4 F or greater

Medications: (check desired lines}, Begin on admission. Non PCN/ B-lactam Allergic patients: Ampicillin 2 gm IV x 1 dose, then 1 gm IV every 4 hours until delivery. Penicillin G 5 million units IV x 1 dose, then 2.5 million units IV every 4 hours until delivery.

PCN/B-lactam allergic patients WITHOUT high risk of anaphylaxis: Cefazolin 2 gm IV x 1 dose, then 1 gm IV every 8 hours untit delivery.

PCN/B-lactam allergic patients WITH high risk for anaphylaxis or B-lactarn resistant GBS: Vancomycin 1 gm IV every 12 hours until delivery. If renal insufficiency, vancomycin IV per pharmacy dosing until delivery.

Antibiotic Allergy Assessment Protocol for B- lactams (Penicillins/Cephalosporins): Consider the nature of the reaction:

Patient is considered to have NO allergy to B- lactams if:

weRKAS 274 of 862

MILLS, AMY

790000259923 [DOB-1135]

[DOB-1] 31y 728946 70000259923

No B-lactam allergy history.

Has only a history of GI distubances: (N/V, diarrhea, constipation).

Has a history of rash with a drug but has tolerated other B-lactam (penicillins or cephalosporins) antibiotics.

Has a histery of unknown teactions but has tolerated other B-lactam antibiotics.

Patient is considered to have a TRUE allergy to B- lactams if: 4.

Has a history of anaphylaxis or respiratory reactions (hypotension, wheezing, respiratory complications, or iaryngeal/face/lip edema or swelling).

Has a history of severe (hard, raised, or painful) rash and HAS NOT tolerated other B- lactam antibiotics since.

Has a history of unknown reactions and HAS NOT tolerated other B-lactam antibiotics since.

CHILD&SIRTH, MOTHER CARE You have had a baby. Itis important to take care of yourself as well as the baby in order to feel better.

Post-partum dlues:;

Many women will experience a form of depression. This ls generally seen about three days after the birth and can last about two weeks. This is caused by the sudden change in your body's harmones, plus the added fife changes of anew baby. The norma! reactions for thls are: crying, irritability, anger, exhaustion, tension, restlessness, and anxlety.

Changes of your uterus:

Your uterus will continue to shrink to its non-pregnant size. You may get your menstrual period in three to eight weeks if you are not breast-feeding, Ifyou are breast-feeding, you may not get your period for six months or longer. You will usuaily ovulate before you gat your period. You may even ovulate without a period. lf you do not want another pregnancy, use some form of birth contro}. Your first period may be much heavier than normal, but your second period should be closer to normal.

Birth control:

If you de not want another pregnancy immediately, use some type of birth control. You can use spermicidal foam and condoms, Talk with your health care provider about the specific birth contro! that would be right for you.

Care of your bottom: Always wipe from front to back after using the bathroom. Change your pads

often to prevent irritation. Do not use tampons until your health care provider says itis okay (usually 6 to 8 weeks), You may shower or take a bath. Donol use bubble bath if you take a tub bath.

Care gf hemorrhoids:

Try using moist lowelettes or medicated towelettes, such as Tucks(TM). Take stool softeners if prescribed. Eat ptenty of fruits, vegetables and whole grain breads and cereals. Drink eight 8-ounce glasses of water each day.

Vagina! discharge:

You will have some vaginal discharge for the next four to six weeks, It is the debris that the uterus sheds after defivery, The discharge will change start out red and change to pinkish to yellow to white. Ht will increase with activity or breastieeding.

Sexual intercourse: You may fesume intercourse after 6 weeks, Que to hormonal changes, your

vagina may be drier than usual, To increase comfart, try using a lubricant, such as K-Y Jelly{TM),

Please follow these Instructions:

» Rest oflen. Try to nap when your baby is napping.

* Ask for help from others.

» Talk about your feelings with a friend or family member,

* Exercise regulady when your health care provider says it's okay. * Take time far yourself,

HYDROCODONE AND ACETAMINOPHEN (Vicodin, Vicodin ES, Lortab, Lortab elixir, Zamicet, Norco, Zydone, Anexsia, Anotar, Bancap HC)

Take this medicine by mouth with food in the following dose: one 5mg/325mg tablet every 4 to 6 hours if needed for pain. Do not take more than 5 tablets per day (24 hours).

This Is a mixture of medicines (hydrocodone and acetaminophen) used ta relieve moderate to severe pain. This medicine may be used for other reasons, as prescribed by your dactar.

Side effects may include:

* sleepiness or dizziness

* upsei stomach, nausea, or vomiting

* constipation

Other side effects may occur, but are not as common. Allergy would show up as: rash or itching, facial or throat swelling, wheezing or shortness of breath. This medicine can be habit forming if used for a long period of time.

At home, please fotlow these instructions: + Never take more of this medicine than prescribed. Too much acetaminophen in your body can cause liver damage. Read the labels of non-prescription medicines before taking them. Many contain acetaminaphen, To avoid an overdose, do not take any other medicines that contain acetaminophen. This medicine may make you dizzy ar drowsy. There is a higher chance you could fall. To prevent falling: + Stand up slowly. if you feel dizzy, haid on to something sturdy until the feeling goes away. * Do not do any activities that require alertness until you know you can safely do so. » Use plenty of light in your house. + Reduce clutler in your home.

Global Patient Safety

The staff of Baptist Health Corbin regards your safety as a priority. We take several precautions to assure your safety during you stay, We require all hospital staff to wear photo identification badges, so all our patients know who we are. Therefore, we ask that you follow these guidelines:

Should you ieave the floor for personal reasons, please follow these guidelines:

Notify staff when leaving the floor.

Go to the nurses’ station to sign out.

When you return to the floor please sign back in on the log book at the nurses station.

If you have not returned to your room by the time you have given us, we will initiate our “Code Purple” to locate you, to assure your safety. “Code Purple” alerts our staff to search for missing patients.

BLOOD TRANSEUSION AND BLOOD PRODUCTS RISKS, BENEFITS, & ALTERNATIVES-If you wish not to receive blood or blood products please request to sign a refusal form, 1) Some surgical procedures may require blood

transfusions or blood products. My doctor has informed me that I may need to have blood products administered during the course of my treatment. 2) It has been explained to me that the administration of blood products invotves the introduction of the product into onc of my veins, commonly in the arm using a needle. I understand that the amount of blood products administered is determined by my doctor based upon my particular needs. 3) It has been explained to me that the administration of blood products may expose me to certain risks. Minor or temporary reactions, such as slight bruising, swelling, or local infection of the area where the needle pierces the skin is not uncommon. Non-serious reactions may include headache, fever, ora mild skin reaction, such as itching or a rash. Rare, but serious reactions are possible such as the transmission of diseases including hepatitis and AIDS, which require lengthy treatment and can be fatal. It has been further explained that while procedures for screening blood products for diseases such as AIDS and hepatitis are effective, these procedures are not perfect and there is a risk of expasure to AIDS, hepatitis, av other bload-borne disease. I have taken all of these sks into consideration and have decided that the benefits of receiving blood products outweigh the risks. 4) I have been made aware of the reasonably available alternatives to the administration of blood products and the risks and benefits of those alternatives including autologous blood transfusion, directed donation and not having any blood products administered. I understand that I may be able to donate one of several units of my own blood to be used during planned elective surgery and that my doctor must determine my ability to donate for myself. This is called autologous transfusion,

If I choose to have an autologous transfusion, I understand that the last unit of blood must be donated one week prior to expected use. I also understand that ] may choose a directed donation. A directed donation means I am allowed to select

ANESTHESIA-I understand that this procedure may require anesthesia. An anesthesiologist has or will explain the anesthesia alternatives. Complications from any type of anesthetic are infrequent, but do occur, Complications are more frequent for patients in poor health than for patients in good health. Complications associated with all types of anesthesia include temporary or permanent damage to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes, nerves, or blood vessels. Drug reaction may occur and may be minor cr serious even requiring resuscitation. Breathing problems may develop.

Headache, back pain, some degree of awareness, infection, nausea and/or vomiting may occur. There are some very serious complications, which are uncommon, but can occur. These include paralysis, brain damage, or death. There are other potential complications depending on your situation; however, it is not possible to advise you of every imaginable complication. The purpase of this is not to frighten you, but to properly inform you. Serious complications are unlikely. The benefits of surgery and anesthesia, except in extreme circumstances, outweigh the potential risks. I agree that the potential benefit of the procedure(s) outweighs the potential risks of anesthesia.

I understand that my procedure is scheduled to be done with one of the following:

O General Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist with or without a CRNA O Monitored Anesthesia Care-possible sedation, monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist or a CRNA, ps? fE Regional Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist or a CRNA (L- yak 7% =

Ol Local Anesthesia-care managed by the Physician and monitored by a registered nurse

O Moderate Sedation-care managed by the Physician and monitored by a registered nurse

1.) Accompanied by a responsible adult.

2.) Nat take public transportation without the presence of another adult.

3.) Not drive a car, ingest alcoholic beverages, or depressant medication without direct permission from the physician, for a minimum of 24 hours.

4.) Not make any important decisions or sign any important documents or checks for 24 to 36 hours

BAPTIST HEALTH Visit##: 70000259923 [DOB-1627] TOBACCO FREE ENVIRONMENT & SMOKING CESSATION = 08: 12/28/1883 Sly F = MRN: 728945 {EID IDEN GNI OE) AON 0 UU MED A a

TOBACCO FREE ENVIRONMENT

Baptist Health supports wellness and health by maintaining a “Tobacco Free” campus environment. Our “Tobaceo Free” environment has been established to minimize adverse health effects to everyone with whom we have contact. This policy applies to all tobacco products inctuding cigarettes, cigars, pipes, herbal tobacco products and chewing tobacco. These items are prohibited from use on Baptist Health’s campus or at any facility owned, leased or operated by Baptist (Excluding Paducah, as there are designated smoking areas). | understand that | will need to communicate with my treating physician or nurse to request nicotine replacement products, If needed. | understand that $ am to remain in my treatment area at all times. | further understand that if | leave my treatment area or any Baptist Health Facility, that § will not be under nursing or medical supervision and may aggravate or worsen my condition and may complicate or interfere with the course of treatment prescribed by my physician.

SMOKING CESSATION

Wellness and Health Promotion: for smokers, those who are around smokers (second-hand smoke), or those who quit smoking and failed.

Smoking cessation is quitting smoking. Smoking is a very difficult habit to break for most pecple. The chemical, nicotine, which you inhale into your lungs from a cigarette, causes your brain to have more dopamine. Dopamine is a chemical that makes you feel good. Nicotine has many more harmful effects on your body. This is why it is so important to stop smoking. Nicotine is addictive, which means when your body is used to having nicotine, and then nicotine isn't there, you feel strong physical cravings and a need to smoke. This is why stopping is so difficult.

Why is smoking bad for me? « Smoking increases your chance for having a heart attack, a stroke and/or cancer.

* Smoking decreases the amount of oxygen that gets to your brain, heart, and other organs. * $moking raises your blood pressure and makes it harder for your blood to circulate throughout your body. * $moking increases acid in your stornach, which leads to ulcers Why is quitting gqaod for me? As soon as you quit smoking, your chances of having a heart attack, stroke, and other diseases start to go down. The longer you do not smoke, the smaller your risk for these diseases and problems.

What is the best way to quit? First, decide in your mind that you are going to quit.

Set a specific date to stop smoking and tell other people that you are going to stop smoking on your quit date.

Talk to your doctor about medications that can be used to help you quit. Over the counter and prescription are avalilabie. Talk to ex-smokers about what hetped them quit.

Join a support group for people who are quitting. Group participation raises your chance of success by eight times. Find friends or family members who are wilting to help you quit or whe will quit smoking with you.

Before your gult date, only allow yourself to smoke in one or two places.

Pay attention te when, where, and with whom you smoke. Notice what things make you feel like smoking.

Avoid the places, situations, and people that cause you to want a cigarette, at feast at first when you are quitting. Make a list of all of the good things that will happen if you quit smoking.

Think of what you will do with the money that you will save by not buying cigarettes.

Begin an exercise program suggested by your doctor.

Throw away all cigarettes, lighters, and matches before your quit date.

For Additional Help, please contact the Kentucky Quit Line: 1-800-Quit Now (1-[PHONE-1628]} or TDY/TDD 1-[PHONE-1629]

VITAMIN B COMPLEX Take this medicine by mouth in the following dose: 1 TAB DAILY

Vitamin B complex includes the following vitamins: thiamine (Vitamin B1), riboflavin (Vitamin B2), niacin (Vitamin 63), pantothenic acid (Vitamin B5), pyridoxine (Vitamin B6), biotm, folic acid, and vitamin G12. Each vitamin performs its own unique function in your body. This supplement may be used in managing diets of people with or at risk for cardiovascular disease, peripheral vascutardisease and cerebrovascular disease. This supplement may be used for other reasons as well, as prescribed by your doctor.

- mild diarrhea

2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL:

In most situations, the medical treatment provided to patients in the Hospital is given by physicians and other providers who are not employees or agents of the Hospital. Such providers include, but are not limited to, anesthesiologists, cardiologists, radiologists, emergency physicians, pathologists surgeons, certified registered nurse anesthetists, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists. These providers may be indepandent or may be employed by other health care organizations. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers or the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers, Charges for such services are established by these providers.

TOBACCO FREE ENVIRONMENT Baptist Health supports wellness and health by maintaining a "Tobacco Free” campus environment. Our “Tobacco Free” environment has been established to minimize adverse health effects to everyone with whom we have contact. This policy applies to all tobacco products including cigarettes, cigars, pipes, herbal tobacco products and chewing tobacco. These items are prohibited from use on Baptist Health's campus or at any facility owned, leased or operated by Baptist (Excluding Paducah, as there are designated smoking areas}. | understand that | will need to communicate with my treating physician or nurse to request nicatine replacement products, if needed, I understand that | am to remain in my treatment area at all times. | further understand that if | leave my treatment area or any Baptist Health Facility, that | will not be under nursing or medical supervision and may aggravate or worsen my condition and may complicate or interfere with the course of treatment prescribed by my physician. SMOKING CESSATION Wellness and Health Promotion; for smokers, those who are around smokers (second-hand smoke), or those who quit smoking and falled. Smoking cessation is quitting smoking. Smoking is a very difficult habit to break for most people. The chemical, nicotine, which you inhale into your lungs from a cigarette, causes your brain to have more dopamine, Dopamine is a chemical that makes you feel good. Nicotine has many more harmful effects on your body. This is why it is so important to stop smoking. Nicotine is addictive, which means when your body is used to having nicotine, and then nicotine isn't there, you fee! strong physical cravings and a need to smoke. This is why stopping is so difficutt. Why is smoking bad for me?

* Smoking increases your chance for having a heart attack, a stroke and/or cancer.

« Smoking decreases the amount of oxygen that gets to your brain, heart, and other organs.

+ Smoking raises your blood pressure and makes it harder for your blood to circulate throughout your body.

* §moking increases acid in your stomach, which leads to ulcers Why is quitting good for me? As soon as you quit smoking, your chances of having a heart attack, stroke, and other diseases start to go down. The ionger you do not smoke, the smaller your risk for these diseases and prablems.

What Is the best way to quit?

* First, decide in your mind that you are going to quit. ¢ Seta specific date to stop smoking and tell other people that you are going to stop smoking on your quit date. * Talk to your doctor about medications that can be used to help you quit. Over the counter and prescription are available. * Talk to ex-smokers about what helped them quit. ¢ Join a support group for people who are quitting. Group participation raises your chance of success by eight times. . Find friends or family members who are willing to help you quit or wha. will quit smoking with you. + Before your quit date, only allow yourself to smoke in one or two places. * Pay attention to when, where, and with whom you smoke. Notice what things make you feel like smoking. - Avoid the places, situations, and people that cause you to want a cigarette, at least at first when you are quitting. . Make a list of all of the good things that will happen if you quit smoking. « Think of what you will do with the money that you will save by not buying cigarettes. . Begin an exercise program suggested by your doctor. * Throw away all cigarettes, lighters, and matches before your quit date. | have reqeived the aboye information about Baptist Health’s Tobacco Free Environment and smoking cessation. Today you have come to the hospital for observation of labor. The results of this visl seem notmal and you may go home.

Aciivity: Return to your usual activities

Other Instructions: - Drink plenty of fluids + Lie on your sides. « Keep bladder ernpty. » Bo not smoke. If you smoke, ptease try not to smoke for at least 2 hours before coming for your next test. Smoking changes the test results.

Movement of the baby: + Anytime you think your baby isn’t moving as much as it should: you need to count the babies movements In the following manner:

Choose a 1 hour time period, during the time your baby is most active. Lay down on your side. Count each time the baby kicks, rolls over or moves In any way, The baby should move at least 6 times, in a hour.If the baby does not move six times in one hour, then come to the hospital. Ga to labor hall and let lhe nurse know that your baby is net moving as it should.

* Water leaks or breaks.

together that are not relleved by walking or resting on your sides.

PRENATAL MULTIVITAMIN,

Take this medicine by mouth in the following dose: 1 multi-vitamin tabletonce a day,

Vitamins are used when the daily diel may not have enough to maintain good health. When you are pregnant, your body needs more vitamins. This vitamin is made especially for use during pregnancy. A side effect may include an upset stomach,

Follow these Instructions:

Take this vitamin with food to avoid an upset stomach.

Do not stop taking this vitamin without talking with your doctor,

Store this medicine away from heat, moisture or direct fight.

If you miss a dose, skip the missed dose and go back to your regular schedule, Do not double the doses.

VITAMIN B COMPLEX Take this medicine by mouth in the following dose: 1 tab daily

Vitamin 8 complex includes the following vilamins: thiamine (Vitamin B1}, riboflavin (Vitamin B2), niacin (Vitamin B3), pantothenic acid (Vitamin BS), pyridoxine (Vitamin B6), biotin, folic acid, and vitamin 812, Each vitamin performs its own unique function in your body. This supplement may be used in managing diets of people with or at risk for cardiovascular disease, peripheral vascular disease and cerebrovascular disease. This supplement may be used for other reasons as well, as preserlbed by your doctor.

Vitamin Dis a vitamin that your body needs. tt is found In food and can be made in your body after exposure to ultraviolet light from the sun. Vitamin D helps your body absorb calcium and phosphorus from your intestines, keeping a normai levet of calcium and phosphorus In your blood, Without enough vitamin D, you may develop osteoporosis and your bones can become weak, thin and brittle. People with kidney, intestinal, or liver problems benefit from a supplement of vitamin D. This supplement may be used for other reasons, as Prescribed by your healthcare provider.

Side effects occur If you take too much vitamin D. This may cause irregular heartbeats, nausea or vomiting, decreased appetile, weakness, and kidney stones.

+ Smoking/Tobacco use can cause Cancer, Heart and Lung Disease.

+ Smoking/Tobacco use is expensive, increases the aging process, and second hand smoke hurts your family and friends.

» Your chances of getting cancer decrease.

«Your chance of heart attack decreases within 24 hours.

«You save money and your taste and smell will improve.

2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL:

In most situations, the medical treatment provided to patients in the Hospital is given by physicians and other providers who are not employees or agents of the Haspital. Such providers include, but are not limited to, anesthesiologists, cardiologists, radiologists, emergency physicians, pathologists surgeons, certified registered nurse anesthetists, nurse practitioners, physician assisiants, surgical assistants and psychologists. These providers may be independent or may be employed by other health care organizations. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers or the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established by these providers.

Hospital; (b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, and physicians; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; and (8) any other persons or entities described in the Hospital's Notice of Privacy Practices. TOBACCO FREE ENVIRONMENT

Baptist Health supparts wellness and health by maintaining a “Tobacco Free” campus environment. Our “Tobacco Free” environment has been established to minimize adverse health effects to everyone with whom we have contact. This policy applies to all tobacco products including cigarettes, cigars, pipes, herbal tobacco products and chewing tobacco. These items are prohibited from use on Baptist Health’s campus or at any facility owned, leased or operated by Baptist (Excluding Paducah, as there are designated smoking areas). | understand that | will need to communicate with my treating physician or nurse to request nicotine replacement products, if needed. | understand that | am to remain in my treatment area at all times. | further understand that if | leave my treatment area or any Baptist Health Facility, that | will not be under nursing or medical supervision and may aggravate or worsen my condition and may complicate or interfere with the course of treatment prescribed by my physician.

SMOKING CESSATION

Wellness and Health Promotion: for smokers, those who are around smokers (second-hand smoke), or those who quit smoking and failed.

Smoking cessation is quitting smoking. Smoking is a very difficult habit to break for most people. The chemical, nicotine, which you inhale into your lungs from a cigarette, causes your brain to have more dopamine. Dopamine is a chemical that makes you feel good. Nicotine has many more harmful effects on your body. This is why it is so important to stop smoking. Nicotine is addictive, which means when your body is used to having nicotine, and then nicotine isn’t there, you feel strong physical cravings and a need to smoke. This is why stopping is so difficult.

Why Is smoking bad for me? *- Smoking increases your chance for having a heart attack, a stroke and/or cancer.

° Smoking decreases the amount of oxygen that gets to your brain, heart, and other organs. : . Smoking raises your bleod pressure and makes it harder for your blood to circulate throughout your body. . Smoking increases acid in your stomach, which leads to ulcers

Why is quitting good for me? As soon as you quit smoking, your chances of having a heart attack, stroke, and other diseases start to go down.

The longer you do not smoke, the smaller your risk for these diseases and problems.

What is the best way to quit?

First, decide in your mind that you are going to quit.

Set a specific date to stop smoking and tell other people that you are going to stop smoking on your quit date.

Talk te your doctor about medications that can be used to help you quit. Over the counter and prescription are available. Talk to ex-smokers about what helped them quit.

Join a support group for people whe are quitting. Group participation raises your chance of success by eight times. Find friends or family members who are willing to help you quit or who will quit smoking with you.

Before your quit date, only allow yourself to smoke in one or two places.

Pay attention to when, where, and with whom you smoke. Notice what things make you feel like smoking.

Avoid the places, situations, and people that cause you to want a cigarette, at least at first when you are quitting. Make 8 list of all of the good things that will happen if you quit smoking.

Think of what you wil do with the money that you will save by not buying cigarettes.

Begin an exercise program suggested by your doctor.

Throw away all cigarettes, lighters, and matches before your quit date.
